  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7792e8c9-0e19-4107-aa71-6c3a2e90b8c4'

They don’t seem to understand that IceWings, the most superior of all dragon tribes, can fix their own problems. When their search leads the dragonets straight into Queen Scarlet’s vicious talons, Winter is grateful to have some help. <div id="review_1455746834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455746834" />
    <a title="Lanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22024407-lanie"><img alt="Lanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208561p2/22024407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455746834?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lanie" href="/user/show/22024407-lanie">Lanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Dragon and epic fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=animal-main-characters">animal-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=children-saving-the-world">children-saving-the-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22024407-lanie?shelf=shitty-parents">shitty-parents</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455746834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1377473784862401919">Not The best of the series. But still quite good. <br/><br/>The writing is wonderful. The world Sutherland has created is vibrant and complex and oh so amazing well thought out for a middle grade series. Or frankly, for ANY epic fantasy series. I loved finally getting to see the icewing culture, even though it was terribly depressing & must be so hard on all those poor Icewing dragonets. (Winter's parents are shit.) I'm loving how far the darkstalker legend has come, has been expanded for the ghost storie</span>
  <span id="freeText1377473784862401919" style="display:none">Not The best of the series. But still quite good. <br /><br />The writing is wonderful. The world Sutherland has created is vibrant and complex and oh so amazing well thought out for a middle grade series. Or frankly, for ANY epic fantasy series. I loved finally getting to see the icewing culture, even though it was terribly depressing &amp; must be so hard on all those poor Icewing dragonets. (Winter's parents are shit.) I'm loving how far the darkstalker legend has come, has been expanded for the ghost stories of the terrified nightwings in book 5. <br /><br />And it was great getting to know these new dragonets better. (Although I still can't figure out why they are suddenly so loyal to each other after knowing each other for like 5 days.) <br /><br />The story itself was well crafted and fun, with hints of "oh my god, this shit is kinda dark, why is it for kids?" Thrown in. Like all the other "wings of fire" books. <br /><br />But, sadly, I didn't find "winter turning" QUITE as enjoyable as pervious books. &amp; again, sadly, I had to give it only 3 stars instead of a super excited 5 or 4. <br /><br />Mostly, do to Winter himself. <br /><br />It was painful, being stuck in his head. :( so sad, because I usually love the tortured soul, angry &amp; sad type heroes. I found him annoying and whiney and mean. Why did moon spend so much time telling how good &amp; great he is? All I saw was a super whiny little bitch. A hateful little bitch. I get that he spent his whole life being told to basically hate all other tribes, (&amp; having unpleasable parents) but come on. It was a bit over the top.... And then the over the top-ness of it was undermined by how quickly he got over it all.<br /><br />Although I did feel how much he missed and loved Hailstorm so that was good. <br /><br />He just wasn't a very likable character. :( I know that they don't always have to be, but I was so looking forward to this book and this character &amp; I felt so let down. :/ <br /><br />It wasn't a bad book really. It just wasn't as great as it could have been. I felt Winter could have been a great character. But really he was just obnoxious. At least I only had to deal with one book in his point of view. The series is still one of my favorites, so I look forward to reading and reviewing the next book "escaping peril" <br /><br />Recommended to fans of dragons, the rest of the series, and lovers of epic fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1377473784862401919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1387808006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1387808006" />
    <a title="Vlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46385201-vlin"><img alt="Vlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440729686p2/46385201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1387808006?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vlin" href="/user/show/46385201-vlin">Vlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1387808006&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1387808006" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15671289411283680243"> The book is out! Thank you, Sutherland, now I can read without worrying on when it is coming out. Anyways, this book features Winter and Moon, the main protagonists. Then there is Qibli, Turtle, and Kinkajou, who are just a bundle of hilarious sidekicks that make the story not torturously boring.<br/><br/> Anyways, it starts out as Winter, an Icewing, with a brother named Hailstorm and a fierce sister named Icicle. Winter and Hailstorm gets assaulted one day by the former wicked queen of Skywings, Scarle</span>
  <span id="freeText15671289411283680243" style="display:none"> The book is out! Thank you, Sutherland, now I can read without worrying on when it is coming out. Anyways, this book features Winter and Moon, the main protagonists. Then there is Qibli, Turtle, and Kinkajou, who are just a bundle of hilarious sidekicks that make the story not torturously boring.<br /><br /> Anyways, it starts out as Winter, an Icewing, with a brother named Hailstorm and a fierce sister named Icicle. Winter and Hailstorm gets assaulted one day by the former wicked queen of Skywings, Scarlet. Hailstorm sacrificed himself, resulting in a search for Winter's brother later on. That's where Moon and her sidekicks come in. She insists that she should help out, but he refused. Eventually, they evened out and went together.<br /><br /> Along the way, there were some few obstacles and dragon fights. Icicle, his sister, was on a quest to find Hailstorm too, but she had another way of doing it. Scarlet had made a deal with her, "Kill Queen Glory to avenge me and your brother will be released." If you're wondering who Glory is, she is Queen of the Rainwings. When Scarlet was Queen of Skywings, she held Glory as her "prisoner." Since Rainwings can spill and spit out acid, she spit on the Queen's face, which now is scarred. The Skywings now think she is dead since she disappeared ever since, so now they have a new Queen, Ruby. Make sense? Anyways, Icicle is hunting for Glory and since the sidekicks and the two protagonists are Glory's allies, they have to find Hailstorm before Winter's sister does. <br /><br /> Eventually, they find Hailstorm. The problem is solved, but then there is another one. During his absence, he was lowered to the lowest circle/rank. And he is the family of a royal bloodline. He has no choice but to slowly rank up with tons of grueling work. I feel like that is a bit unfair and all that trouble was for nothing.<br /><br /> To sum it up, I would give this story four stars. It did have some mistakes, but not every book is perfect! I recommend this series to everyone. Good luck on reading it! I hope you have as much as a good experience I had.<br /><br />*Sorry if I have spelling or grammar mistakes. I'm not the best at those two subjects. :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="15671289411283680243" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1334026241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1334026241" />
    <a title="Aelvana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana"><img alt="Aelvana" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1334026241?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aelvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aelvana" href="/user/show/33911745-aelvana">Aelvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334026241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17382387733994320507">Winter is proud to be an IceWing---though his family is constantly disappointed in how he's not as good as his sister, Icicle, or his brother, Hailstorm. It gets even worse when Hailstorm is captured (also Winter's fault). Now that Winter knows Hailstorm is still alive, and that there might be a chance to rescue him, he'll stop at nothing to get his brother back. If only he didn't have to put up with the other dragons of his winglet, who insist on calling him "friend" . . .<br/><br/>I'm continually impres</span>
  <span id="freeText17382387733994320507" style="display:none">Winter is proud to be an IceWing---though his family is constantly disappointed in how he's not as good as his sister, Icicle, or his brother, Hailstorm. It gets even worse when Hailstorm is captured (also Winter's fault). Now that Winter knows Hailstorm is still alive, and that there might be a chance to rescue him, he'll stop at nothing to get his brother back. If only he didn't have to put up with the other dragons of his winglet, who insist on calling him "friend" . . .<br /><br />I'm continually impressed at how well Tui T. Sutherland draws her characters. This second set of dragonets is markedly different from the original five, but if anything I think I like them more. This particular volume is told from Winter's point of view. Winter is complex: on the one hand, he's cold and stuck-up, but seeing things from his point of view really highlights his insecurities and how he's starting to like the others. And how much he hates liking the others because that's not a proper IceWing thing to feel. And how he feels like a failure as an IceWing, anyway, but he's going to try his best to be a good one.<br /><br />I love what develops between Winter and Hailstorm, particularly with how the end mirrors the beginning in some surprising ways. And what happened to poor Hailstorm (ouch). <br /><br />The humor is, as usual, spot-on. Winter makes a particularly funny lead because he's so earnest in his insistence that these are NOT his "friends" and he does NOT like non-IceWings and why won't they just let him go off and hunt for Hailstorm by himself? And then he still humbles himself to listen to reason from Qibli or puts himself out to help them, because it's the right thing to do, and gets all flustered whenever anyone tries to thank him for it. <br /><br />I also like the additional details about the history of the various tribes (mostly the NightWing/IceWing rivalry in this one), which helps flesh out the past a bit more. And in the other direction, it's equally interesting to see how the hard-won peace is working out for everyone. The conclusion to The Brightest Night was in some ways a happily-ever-after ending, but these books help to underscore that it really is more than just winning a battle or a throne to end a war. <br /><br />All in all, it's almost a shame I read this so close to publication, because now I have to wait for the next one. And that will be rather annoying, because there were some really juicy teases at the very end leading into the next book . . . I rate this book Highly Recommended.<br /><br />See my reviews and more at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://offtheshelfreviews.wordpress.com">http://offtheshelfreviews.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17382387733994320507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24358444-winter-turning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42972061-merie-shen?shelf=most-favorite-of-all">most-favorite-of-all</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2712419106&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2712419106" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15863866677423696462">AAAAAAGHHHHHHH<br/><br/> Oh, sorry. *coughs* Sorry, this book was SO GOOD I kind of HAD to start screaming incoherently in your faces. :) <br/><br/> I'm so glad I finally read Winter's story!! (This time I read it before my sister... *smug smile*) Winter Turning is undoubtedly my favorite book in the entire Wings of Fire series... which is saying a lot, because I've never been able to choose a favorite. They're literally all that good. But I've never been able to choose a favorite dragonet either, and it's kind of </span>
  <span id="freeText15863866677423696462" style="display:none">AAAAAAGHHHHHHH<br /><br /> Oh, sorry. *coughs* Sorry, this book was SO GOOD I kind of HAD to start screaming incoherently in your faces. :) <br /><br /> I'm so glad I finally read Winter's story!! (This time I read it before my sister... *smug smile*) Winter Turning is undoubtedly my favorite book in the entire Wings of Fire series... which is saying a lot, because I've never been able to choose a favorite. They're literally all that good. But I've never been able to choose a favorite dragonet either, and it's kind of obvious by now that Winter is by far my favorite.<br /><br /> His memories about his life in the Ice Kingdom were so honest and real and raw, showing us how they changed him into the dragon he is today. His character arc was done soooooo wellllll. His friendship with Qibli was so true and brotherly, and then there was Kinkajou, whom he learned to respect, and then there was Moon. Ahhh... well <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I know how this love triangle ends, so it was very, very painful for me to read Winter and his thoughts about Moon, because... erghh... my heart.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And then there were all these awesome cameos from characters we know and love-- Glory, Deathbringer, Riptide (RIPTIDE), Squid... okay, I don't really love Squid, but he was kind of hilarious... UGH I love this book so much.<br /><br /> The IceWing world was amazing. Of course, there were a lot of problems with it; its hierarchy was the reason for Winter's miserable life, but the way Sutherland built it, it was so much stronger and clearer and deeper, I think, than any of the other tribe kingdoms. While it definitely wasn't as dark as the Night Kingdom-- I mean, the Ice Kingdom was given the gift of light-- it was still cold and a little cruel. It was so glittery and light-filled on the outside, but it still gave me the shivers. <br /><br /> All in all, I give this book a million stars out of five. :) It deserves that much. Winter deserves that much. &lt;3 </span>
  <a data-text-id="15863866677423696462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Ehrehn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66041340-ehrehn"><img alt="Ehrehn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544831843p2/66041340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1961503016?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ehrehn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ehrehn" href="/user/show/66041340-ehrehn">Ehrehn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ehrehn by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/66289738-jedi-master-megan">Jedi Master Megan</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66041340-ehrehn?shelf=honorable-mentions">honorable-mentions</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961503016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18243743962773274506">This book was almost as good at the last one. I loved it. I love how different Winter's and Moon's personalities are which makes Winter's point of view on things way different. I feel like many people can connect to Winter. Like how Winter always wants to impress his parents and he always thinks he's not good enough. Many people feel those emotions everyday. Also, the fact that Winter is very confused about his emotions towards Moon. At first, I thought Winter was going to be a very cliche chara</span>
  <span id="freeText18243743962773274506" style="display:none">This book was almost as good at the last one. I loved it. I love how different Winter's and Moon's personalities are which makes Winter's point of view on things way different. I feel like many people can connect to Winter. Like how Winter always wants to impress his parents and he always thinks he's not good enough. Many people feel those emotions everyday. Also, the fact that Winter is very confused about his emotions towards Moon. At first, I thought Winter was going to be a very cliche character since he's always angry and he's a huge jerk in the first book. But now I understand he reasons for him being like that and so does Moon. Moon is always trying to encourage him and always saying he's one of the bravest dragons in the land. I find that really cute and adorable. Winter's character development is really amazing throughout this book, he changes from caring what circle he's in to caring about his friends. I honestly think this is so much more compelling to read just because of the love triangle between Winter, Moon, and Qibli. I also don't really know if I'll enjoy the next book because it's about Peril and I don't really like her ;-;</span>
  <a data-text-id="18243743962773274506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1409978167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409978167" />
    <a title="Eli Lenett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35011993-eli-lenett"><img alt="Eli Lenett" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1409978167?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eli Lenett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eli Lenett" href="/user/show/35011993-eli-lenett">Eli Lenett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1409978167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer475911918168677732">Winter turning is a very good entry in the New Wings of Fire series, and should definitely be read. The book leaves off of a huge cliffhanger from the last book, Moon Rising, and it doesn't take much for the action to start up again. One of my favorite things about the book is the characters. Throughout the whole Wings of Fire series this realism and attachment has been there. From the first book, making me feel for what happened to Clay, to Winter Turning, where I felt Winter's struggles. Besid</span>
  <span id="freeText475911918168677732" style="display:none">Winter turning is a very good entry in the New Wings of Fire series, and should definitely be read. The book leaves off of a huge cliffhanger from the last book, Moon Rising, and it doesn't take much for the action to start up again. One of my favorite things about the book is the characters. Throughout the whole Wings of Fire series this realism and attachment has been there. From the first book, making me feel for what happened to Clay, to Winter Turning, where I felt Winter's struggles. Besides the realism that this book has, the action is as fresh and constant as ever. Still, Winter Turning is more focused o Winter's struggles, relationships, and story than the fights he has been in. With one of the best plots I have ever seen in a book, outstanding and interesting characters, and nonstop action, Winter Turning "Turns Out" to be a fantastic book, possibly even the best I have ever read, and I definitely recommend this book to readers of all ages!</span>
  <a data-text-id="475911918168677732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8372287368668847677" style="display:none">Winter was a far more enjoyable character when you weren't stuck in his head.  I would have preferred a story from Kinkajou's perspective (namely because I never know what she's thinking or will say next, so she's an exciting conundrum).<br /><br />Winter spent the entire book brooding like a stereotypical, downtrodden, YA male protagonist, and arguing why the idiotic rules in place in his society are more important than the friends how have proven their loyalty and devotion to him time and time again.  I genuinely do not think Winter grew enough to warrant his own perspective book, and the only truly good things that came out of this book were FINALLY getting to see the IceWing kingdom and some other spoilery stuff that happened that was awesome.<br /><br />I still rated this book 4 stars because I didn't hate his character, and he did have a bit of growth, but it was so suddenly at the end, that it felt minutely forced for him to get thrown back into the main plot.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14903533420214026246">"Winter Turning" is by far the best book in the series so far. Winter is a believable character, although he's difficult to like. The magic and the quest themes are pretty standard, but in this book they're used to explore character growth. Kiddo is still reading these and loving them, and I typically read along just so that we can discuss it together. I would have finished this one even if he hadn't, though.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Megan McGlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88358085-megan-mcglin"><img alt="Megan McGlin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2765504283?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan McGlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan McGlin" href="/user/show/88358085-megan-mcglin">Megan McGlin</a>
      </span>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2765504283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13901816627697198749">Name: Megan McGlin<br/><br/>Book title: <i>Winter Turning: Wings of Fire #7</i><br/><br/>Personal response: I really enjoyed reading the book <i>Winter Turning Wings of Fire </i>. It is the seventh book out of the wings of fire series and this book is one of the best. It deals with a lot of drama just like all the other books in the series. This is a book about the backstory of Winter and how he came about in Moon's life and how he joined Jade Mountain Academy. There is not that much history behind the icewings, but this book re</span>
  <span id="freeText13901816627697198749" style="display:none">Name: Megan McGlin<br /><br />Book title: <i>Winter Turning: Wings of Fire #7</i><br /><br />Personal response: I really enjoyed reading the book <i>Winter Turning Wings of Fire </i>. It is the seventh book out of the wings of fire series and this book is one of the best. It deals with a lot of drama just like all the other books in the series. This is a book about the backstory of Winter and how he came about in Moon's life and how he joined Jade Mountain Academy. There is not that much history behind the icewings, but this book really explains the icewing history. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Plot: Winter is an icewing prince who can be a spoiled little brat sometimes who always gets his way. He is forced to go to Jade Mountain Academy where all dragons of every tribe try to create peace between each other. Icewings are usually described as one of the cold-hearted dragons in all of Phyria, but is Winter actually cold-hearted or will he let someone in his life change that for him?<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Recommendations: I recommend this book to anybody that enjoys fantasy and adventure and I also recommend the series also. This book was very interesting to learn the backstory of winter and also some of the icewing history.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13901816627697198749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8951048091590532634">This book was about Winter and his growth as a character. As we knew, he wouldn't be leaving his friends for long and although you might say that's a spoiler, it's really not. If you're honest, you knew he wasn't going to stay there. But how it all panned out and what made him leave is full of fun plot twists that I didn't see coming! We get a lot of answers to some questions that we will need to know going forward while we learn more about Winter's parents and why it must have sucked to have be</span>
  <span id="freeText8951048091590532634" style="display:none">This book was about Winter and his growth as a character. As we knew, he wouldn't be leaving his friends for long and although you might say that's a spoiler, it's really not. If you're honest, you knew he wasn't going to stay there. But how it all panned out and what made him leave is full of fun plot twists that I didn't see coming! We get a lot of answers to some questions that we will need to know going forward while we learn more about Winter's parents and why it must have sucked to have been an Ice Wing! The palace sounds beautiful though. And although I know they're gonna make an animated series of this, the adult in me would love to see a million dollar Harry Potter/Lord of the Rings type film of these books. I can only imagine the artistic creations of the kingdoms someone could have fun with. I'd totally be on board with that. I now have all my kids reading this series.</span>

The friendships feel very real.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f+p3Q/AIMCZEqMI7xabQYUIu9bLzBme89AktaZp3/tgXU+a+SsY/B39VYka+QZzPUZQULnC7U3tqe5Altnmyew==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NF6O3CmdJ3oVgmFumFtr9fXQO4aEq7wEvgref5bfE59c5x8hk1MoWy5/wRPjvCdb5mraGgcWiMMgeGMzutFfPA==')})
  }

<a href="/author/show/374504.Tui_T_Sutherland">Tui T. Sutherland

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10221259727667571737">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br/><br/>Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br/><br/>I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay</span>
  <span id="freeText10221259727667571737" style="display:none">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br /><br />Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br /><br />I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay; Miami, Florida; and Santo Domingo, Dominican Republic, before moving to New Jersey in high school, where I started doing theatre—mostly backstage work, because (a) it was fun, and (b) you got to hang out in the dark with cute boys. (Er, I mean . . . because it was artistically fulfilling, yes.)<br /><br />I graduated from Williams College in ’98 and I currently live in Boston with my husband, my perfect new baby, and my adorable yoodle Sunshine (what’s a yoodle? A puppy that’s three-quarters poodle and one-quarter Yorkshire terrier, of course!).<br /><br />Much to my parents’ relief, I abandoned my theatrical aspirations after college for the far more stable and lucrative career of fiction writing.<br /><br />My first two official books were beginning readers, part of Grosset &amp; Dunlap’s “First Friends” series for kids learning to read. MEET MO AND ELLA is tough to find now, but FUN WITH MO AND ELLA should still be out there somewhere.<br /><br />My first novel for teenagers was THIS MUST BE LOVE, which retells Shakespeare’s play A Midsummer Night’s Dream in a modern-day high school, from the POV of the two heroines, Hermia and Helena.<br /><br />And now I'm writing in a new project called SEEKERS! It's a children's book series that I'm writing with Erin Hunter. Check out my blog to find out more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10221259727667571737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

Moonwatcher isn’t sure how she feels about school, however. Hidden in the rainforest for most of her life, the young NightWing has an awful secret. She can read minds, and even see the future. Living in a cave with dozens of other dragons is noisy, exhausting--and dangerous. In just a few days, Moon finds herself overwhelmed by her secret powers and bombarded by strange thoughts, including those of a mysterious dragon who might be a terrible enemy.
